## management-governance / 04_ownership-and-insider-behavior.md

_Source: `04_ownership-and-insider-behavior.md`_

# Ownership & Insider Behavior — NIVABUPA

**Jurisdiction:** India (NSE: NIVABUPA). Reporting standard: IFRS 17 (primary) and Ind AS. Currency: INR. Fiscal year ends 31 March.

**Data note:** The primary ownership sources in the data pool are S&P Global Market Intelligence (Capital IQ) Public Ownership Summary and Private Ownership exports (dated Jun-04-2026) and the Board Members file (Jun-04-2026). These are data-vendor sources (source hierarchy tier 5) rather than primary SEBI LODR shareholding-pattern filings (tier 4). The SEBI LODR quarterly shareholding-pattern filing and SAST / PIT insider-transaction disclosures are NOT in the data pool. Where the vendor data aligns with transcript disclosures, it is treated as Amber-confidence (3/5). The absence of SEBI LODR primary filings prevents firing any RF-OWN red flags per the red-flag gating rule (F20); ownership figures from the vendor file are reported as labeled context only.

All ownership percentages below are sourced from the S&P Global Market Intelligence Public Ownership Summary export (data as of Jun-03/04-2026, position dates as noted per holder) and are labeled as vendor-sourced / unverified against primary SEBI LODR filing.

---

## 1. Ownership

| Holder | % Held | Shares Held | Share Class | Bought or Granted? | Source |
|---|---:|---:|---|---|---|
| The British United Provident Association Limited (Bupa Group, UK) | 55.35% | 1,022,690,470 | Ordinary equity | Bought (corporate parent stake, investment in prior transaction — pre-IPO; BUPA Investments Overseas Limited made a prior investment Jan-05-2015 of ~USD 30.84 mn and subsequent top-ups) | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary, position date Dec-31-2024 (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Fettle Tone LLP (Fairfax-linked entity; also referred to as FIH Mauritius Investments Ltd in transcripts) | 7.91% | 146,202,091 | Ordinary equity | Bought (acquired the former Max India promoter stake through Fettle Tone / True North / Fairfax network in a prior transaction; True North Managers LLP made a transaction Feb-26-2019 of ~USD 71.85 mn; Bupa Insurance Limited made a separate transaction Sep-29-2023 of ~USD 325 mn) | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary, position date Jun-02-2025 (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Total promoter bloc (Bupa + Fettle Tone) | ~63.3% | ~1,168,892,561 | Ordinary equity | Bought | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary, estimated by summing both strategic holders (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Individuals / Insiders (aggregate 6 holders per vendor data) | 0.88% | 16,170,367 | Ordinary equity | Mix — likely granted as ESOPs/restricted units for management; no open-market purchase disclosed in available data | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| DSP BlackRock Investment Managers Pvt. Ltd. | 3.21% | 59,242,719 | Ordinary equity | Bought (institutional) | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary, position date Apr-30-2026 (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Motilal Oswal Financial Services, Investment Arm | 2.62% | 48,399,106 | Ordinary equity | Bought (institutional) | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary, position date Dec-31-2024 (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Nippon Life India Asset Management Limited | 2.52% | 46,629,930 | Ordinary equity | Bought (institutional) | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary, position date Apr-30-2026 (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Franklin Resources (various funds) | 2.40% (estimated) | ~44.3 mn | Ordinary equity | Bought (net buyer, increased by 4.77 mn shares in most recent period) | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary, Top Buyers table (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Public and other (retail float) | 7.82% | 144,520,881 | Ordinary equity | Bought | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Total institutions (33 holders per vendor data) | 26.00% | 480,395,134 | Ordinary equity | Bought | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary (vendor-sourced, unverified) |

**Total insider ownership** (management + executive directors as a class, per vendor data "Individuals/Insiders"): approximately **0.88%** of total shares outstanding — a token holding of 16.17 million shares with a market value of roughly INR 1,359 million (INR ~136 crores at the Jun-03-2026 price of INR 84.48 per share). Vendor data does not separately name which individuals hold these shares; no primary SEBI LODR filing is available to identify the individual holders or verify whether any holding was built through open-market purchase versus ESOP grant.

**The effective controlling bloc** is the two institutional promoters, Bupa Group (UK) and Fettle Tone LLP (Fairfax-linked), together holding approximately 63.3% of total equity, making this a controlled company. The remaining 36.7% is split between institutional investors (26.0%), public / retail float (7.82%), and management insiders (0.88%).

**Context on share count:** Total shares outstanding 1,847,757,271 per the vendor data. This reflects the post-IPO (November 2024 listing) count.

---

## 2. Insider Transactions (last 12 months)

**Important note (red-flag gating, F20):** The SEBI PIT / SAST insider-transaction disclosures are NOT in the data pool. The vendor data (S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary, position window Dec-31-2025 to Mar-31-2026 and Mar-04-2026 to Jun-04-2026) is the only available source. Per module rules, this caps the "recent insider behavior" component to **Low-confidence / Insufficient-Data** and no RF-OWN red flag may be triggered from this source alone.

| Period | Insider Category | Buy / Sell | Shares | Notes | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---:|---|
| Dec-31-2025 to Mar-31-2026 | Individuals / Insiders (aggregate 6 holders) | Neutral | 0 new, 0 increased, 0 decreased | No position changes in this window; same 6 holders, same 16,170,367 shares | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Mar-04-2026 to Jun-04-2026 | Individuals / Insiders (aggregate) | Neutral | 0 buys, 0 sells | No transactions recorded in this window | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Dec-31-2025 to Mar-31-2026 | Institutional buyers | Net buying | +22,675,621 shares added across 16 holders | Broad-based net buying from institutions; 1 new holder (103,747 shares); 4 holders reduced (−8,564,544) | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Dec-31-2025 to Mar-31-2026 | Other Strategic Holders (Bupa + Fettle Tone + 1 other) | Neutral | 0 changes | Promoter bloc unchanged across this window | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary (vendor-sourced, unverified) |

**Top institutional buyers (most recent period):**
- Franklin Resources, Inc.: +4,769,253 shares (now 44,274,645 total; a conviction add from a global value manager)
- Tata Asset Management: +1,650,705 shares
- Bajaj Finserv Asset Management: +587,921 shares
- Axis AMC: +296,628 shares

**Top institutional sellers (most recent period):**
- DSP BlackRock: −6,372,726 shares (highest-volume seller, though still holds 59.24 mn shares; a partial trim, not an exit)
- Morgan Stanley Investment Management: −111,034 shares (minor)
- Groww AMC: −64,060 shares (minor)

**Net insider activity:** Neutral / no transaction. Management insiders (the 6 individuals holding 0.88% of total) made zero open-market transactions in either the December 2025 – March 2026 or the March 2026 – June 2026 window per vendor data. This is consistent with either post-IPO lock-in periods still applying to ESOP-derived shares, or the absence of any open-market conviction buy from management. It cannot be interpreted as insider selling (no sales), but it also cannot be interpreted as conviction buying. The absence of insider transactions is classified as **Neutral**.

No 10b5-1 equivalent (SEBI pre-clearance plan) disclosures appear in available data. Option exercises are not separately identified; the vendor data does not break down the nature of individual / insider positions. SEBI PIT disclosures (the Indian equivalent of Form 4) are not in the pool.

## 3. Pledging & Encumbrance

| Insider / Promoter | Shares Pledged | % of Their Holding | Source |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| Bupa Group (The British United Provident Association Limited) | Not disclosed | Not assessable | SEBI LODR shareholding-pattern filing not in pool; no transcript reference to pledge; no mention in vendor data |
| Fettle Tone LLP | Not disclosed | Not assessable | Same as above |
| Management insiders (aggregate) | Not disclosed | Not assessable | Same as above |

**No pledging disclosed in any source in the data pool.** Six quarterly earnings call transcripts (Q2 FY25 through Q4 FY26, November 2024 – May 2026) contain zero references to promoter pledging or share encumbrance. The disqualifier scan (business-model/01_disqualifier-scan.md) also found no pledge reference and noted that the structure of Bupa Singapore Holdings / The British United Provident Association Limited as a global corporate parent (not a leveraged promoter-household) is inconsistent with typical pledge structures. This is a structural observation, not a verified absence from a primary filing.

**Red-flag gating rule (F20) applies:** A pool filing (SEBI LODR shareholding-pattern) is required to fire RF-OWN-001 (pledge above threshold) or RF-OWN-002 (pledge up QoQ). Neither is triggered. The absence of the primary filing is noted as a data gap. There is no affirmative evidence of pledging from any source.

**Verdict on pledging:** No pledging disclosed. Structural argument against material pledging (Bupa is a global insurer, not a leveraged promoter). But the SEBI LODR primary filing has not been reviewed — pledging status cannot be conclusively verified as zero. Mark as "Insufficient Data — no pool filing confirming either way."

---

## 4. Control Structure

| Feature | Detail | Source |
|---|---|---|
| Dual-class / super-voting shares | None identified. Niva Bupa has a single class of ordinary equity shares. No dual-class structure, super-voting rights, or differential voting rights are mentioned in any transcript or vendor filing. | Q4 FY26 transcript (no dual-class reference); S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary — single ordinary equity class listed (vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Controlled-company status | Yes — effectively controlled. Bupa Group alone holds 55.35%; together with Fettle Tone LLP (~7.91%), the promoter bloc controls approximately 63.3% of voting equity. This is a standard promoter-dominated structure under Indian company law. | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary (vendor-sourced, unverified); consistent with all transcript references to "promoter" structure |
| Shareholder bloc with board-nomination rights | Bupa Group's nominee on the board: David Martin Fletcher (Non-Executive Director since Oct-28-2014; Bupa Group Chief Risk Officer). Roger William John Davis (Non-Executive Director since Jan-29-2026; Former Independent Chairman of the British United Provident Association Limited). Two Bupa-affiliated nominees on the board out of 7 total board members. Fettle Tone / Fairfax: not separately identified on board per vendor data, but the promoter bloc collectively influences board appointment under Ind AS governance norms for majority-controlled companies. | S&P Global MI Board Members export (Jun-04-2026, vendor-sourced, unverified) |
| Foreign promoter / FDI ownership | Bupa Singapore Holdings Pte Ltd / The British United Provident Association Limited is a foreign corporate promoter. The Insurance Amendment Bill referenced in Q3 FY26 (Jan 2026) raised FDI in insurance to 100% — removing the previous cap that constrained Bupa's stake. This is a strategic positive for the promoter but neutral for minority shareholders. | Q3 FY26 transcript, Jan 29, 2026, p.5 (100% FDI insurance amendment) |
| Controlling-owner objective alignment (Filter 6, §24) | Bupa Group is a private UK health-services organization with a clear, single-sector focus on health insurance and care globally. Its objective in Niva Bupa is to build a profitable health insurer in the world's fastest-growing health insurance market — directly aligned with Niva Bupa shareholders' goal of per-share value creation. This is not a government owner, not a parent redirecting economics to a competing vehicle (Bupa's primary business outside India is in markets where Niva Bupa does not compete), and not a sprawling conglomerate. RF-OWN-004 does NOT apply. Fettle Tone / Fairfax: Fairfax is a diversified insurance holding company; its stake in Niva Bupa is a financial investment, not an operational control situation — also not RF-OWN-004. The minority shareholder risk is the standard listed-subsidiary risk of an institutional promoter: the promoter may make decisions that optimize for the group (e.g., related-party transactions at less-than-arm's-length pricing with Bupa Singapore) rather than maximize Niva Bupa's per-share value. This risk is flagged in business-model/11_capital-allocation-governance.md (RPT with Bupa Singapore cannot be sized from available data — no Annual Report). It is a data gap, not a confirmed conflict. | Q4 FY26 transcript, May 8, 2026; business-model/11_capital-allocation-governance.md (RPT note absent from data pool); S&P Global MI Board Members (vendor-sourced, unverified) |

**Unaligned-owner test (CLAUDE.md §24, Filter 6):** RF-OWN-004 does NOT apply. Bupa Group is a private, single-sector health-care and insurance organization. Its ownership objective — building a scaled, profitable health insurer in India — is materially aligned with Niva Bupa minority shareholders' objective. Neither the government-control criterion, the listed-subsidiary-of-a-value-maximizing-parent criterion, nor the sprawling-conglomerate criterion applies. The persistent-cheapness / value-trap risk from Filter 6 does not apply here. However, the RPT concern (Bupa charging Niva Bupa for brand, technology, or reinsurance services at above-market rates) is a real but unquantified related-party risk that is structurally present in any insurer that has a global parent with overlapping capabilities. This is a data gap, not a structural misalignment of objectives.

---

## 4A. Market Conduct

| Signal | Detail | Source |
|---|---|---|
| Insider buys/sells vs subsequent results (timing) | No insider transactions (buys or sells) are disclosed in the available data for any period post-IPO. The vendor data shows 0 insider buy/sell transactions from Mar-04-2026 to Jun-04-2026 and 0 changes to insider positions from Dec-31-2025 to Mar-31-2026. Without any transactions, there is no timing to evaluate. SEBI PIT disclosures (the Indian equivalent of Form 4) are not in the pool and cannot be cross-checked. | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary (vendor-sourced, unverified); SEBI PIT not in pool |
| Unusual price/volume before announcements | Not assessable. No exchange clarification notices, SEBI surveillance alerts, or price-query responses are in the data pool. No transcript references unusual pre-announcement trading. | Not in pool; cannot be assessed |
| Exchange clarification sought for a price move | Not disclosed in any data pool source. The company is relatively recently listed (November 2024 IPO), so the full window of quarterly price behavior has not yet been documented. | Not in pool |
| Institutional (FII/DII/MF) holding trend; sharp high-quality-holder exit | Net institutional buying in the most recent window (Dec-31-2025 to Mar-31-2026): 16 holders increased, 4 reduced, 0 exited entirely. Franklin Resources added 4.77 mn shares — the largest single add, a positive quality-holder signal. DSP BlackRock trimmed by 6.37 mn shares — the largest single reduction; DSP still holds 59.24 mn shares (3.21% of total), so this is a partial trim rather than a conviction exit. No sharp exit by a high-quality holder is visible. | S&P Global MI Public Ownership Summary, Top Buyers and Sellers table (vendor-sourced, unverified) |

No market-conduct red flag (RF-MKT-001 or RF-MKT-002) can be triggered from available data — the SEBI PIT filing is not in the pool, and no insider selling before weak results or unusual pre-announcement activity appears in any transcript or vendor source. Per F20 gating rule, this remains **Insufficient Data** for market-conduct assessment.

---

## 5. Ownership / Insider Read

Management holds approximately 0.88% of shares — a minimal stake, with no evidence of open-market buying from any available source. All available data is consistent with this stake being accumulated through ESOPs or grants rather than cash purchase, though the primary SEBI LODR filing (which would confirm this) is absent. The two institutional promoters — Bupa Group (UK) at 55.35% and Fettle Tone / Fairfax at ~7.91% — hold a combined ~63.3% and control the company outright; Bupa's long-term objective (building a scaled India health insurer) is broadly aligned with minority holders, but the structurally unverifiable risk of RPT value leakage through Bupa brand, technology, or reinsurance fees prevents a clean sign-off on promoter alignment. The net insider signal is neutral: zero transactions, zero pledging disclosed, zero promoter bloc changes in the most recent window — and an institutionally net-buying market (16 new or increased institutional positions vs 4 reduced), with Franklin Resources making the largest single add.

## management-governance / 05_board-and-shareholder-rights.md

_Source: `05_board-and-shareholder-rights.md`_

# Board & Shareholder Rights — NIVABUPA

**Ticker:** NIVABUPA (NSE / BSE)
**Date:** 2026-06-22
**Agent:** 05_board-and-shareholder-rights
**Jurisdiction:** India — SEBI LODR + IRDAI (standalone health insurer, Ind AS / IFRS 17)
**Reporting currency:** INR. Fiscal year ends 31 March.

**Partial-data notice:** The AGM Notice, Corporate Governance Report (proxy-equivalent), Board's Report remuneration section, Secretarial Audit Report, SEBI LODR shareholding-pattern filings, SEBI PIT insider-trade disclosures, and the IRDAI statutory Annual Report with Notes to Accounts are all absent from the data pool. Board composition and committee membership are sourced from the Capital IQ Board Members export (vendor data, confidence 3/5). AGM voting results, related-party transaction quantum (Ind AS 24 Note), and minority-vote outcomes cannot be assessed. All caps per the partial-data rules in MODULE_RULES.md apply. See Section 5 (Minority-Shareholder Protection Read) for impact.

## 1. Board Composition

The board, based on the Capital IQ Board Members export (current as of ~June 2026), has nine directors.

| Feature | Detail | Source |
|---|---|---|
| Board size | 9 directors | Capital IQ Board Members, current (~Jun 2026) |
| Director roster | Milind G. Barve (Independent Chairman); Krishnan Ramachandran (MD, CEO & ED); Vishwanath Mahendra (CFO & ED); Ankur Kharbanda (Deputy CEO & ED); David Martin Fletcher (Non-Executive Director, Bupa-nominated); Roger William John Davis (Non-Executive Director, Bupa-nominated); Geeta Dutta Goel (Independent Director); Mohit Gupta (Independent Director); Vivek Anant Karve (Additional Independent Director) | Capital IQ Board Members, current (~Jun 2026) |
| Executive (internal) directors | 3: Ramachandran (CEO), Mahendra (CFO), Kharbanda (Deputy CEO) | Capital IQ Board Members, current (~Jun 2026) |
| Promoter-nominated non-executive directors | 2: Fletcher (Bupa Group Chief Risk Officer since 2017; on this board since 2014); Davis (former Bupa Independent Non-Exec since 2015; appointed to NIVABUPA board Jan 29, 2026) | Capital IQ Board Members, current (~Jun 2026) |

| Independent directors (% of total) | 44% (4 of 9) | Calculated from Capital IQ Board Members |
| Non-executive directors (% of total) | 67% (6 of 9: 4 independent + 2 Bupa-nominated) | Calculated from Capital IQ Board Members |
| True independence: Fletcher & Davis | Not independent. Fletcher is Bupa Group Chief Risk Officer — he is a senior employee of the controlling promoter (Bupa, 55.35% holder). Davis joined in Jan 2026 and is former Bupa Independent Non-Exec Chairman and former Chairman of Bupa Finance plc — he has extensive Bupa-linked affiliation. Neither qualifies as independent under true-independence criteria, even if they carry an "external" role classification. The two Bupa NEDs effectively represent promoter interests. | Capital IQ Board Members (backgrounds); web-sourced background (labeled below) |
| Chair / CEO split? | Yes — Independent Chairman (Barve) is separate from the CEO (Ramachandran). This is a positive structural feature. | Capital IQ Board Members, current (~Jun 2026) |

| Compensation (Remuneration) Committee | Fletcher and Goel are listed as Compensation Committee members. Same limitation: Fletcher is Bupa-nominated and his presence reduces true independence of this committee. | Capital IQ Board Members |
| Nominating / Nomination Committee | Fletcher and Goel are listed as Nominating Committee members. Same limitation. | Capital IQ Board Members |
| Risk Committee | Fletcher is listed as Chairman of the Risk Committee. This creates a structural conflict: Bupa's own Group CRO chairs the risk oversight body of a company in which Bupa holds 55.35%. Risk Committee independence is compromised. | Capital IQ Board Members |
| Investment Committee | Ramachandran (CEO), Mahendra (CFO), and Jain (CIO) are listed as Investment Committee members. This is management-dominated and does not include independent directors per available data. | Capital IQ Board Members / Professionals export |
| Sector overlay (IRDAI) | IRDAI requires insurers to have at least 50% of the board as non-executive directors and mandates appointment of independent directors. The board satisfies the non-executive majority (67%). Whether it satisfies IRDAI's specific independent-director count requirement is not verifiable without the CG Report. | Inference from IRDAI Insurance Companies Corporate Governance Guidelines (labeled as inference) |

**Board-independence summary (plain read):** On paper, 44% of the board (4/9) are labelled independent and 67% are non-executive. But the two Bupa-nominated directors (Fletcher and Davis) are not truly independent — Fletcher is a senior Bupa employee with a 10+ year directorship, and Davis has deep Bupa-group history. If the Audit, Compensation, and Nomination committees each include Fletcher, the true independence of all three is compromised. Barve (Independent Chairman, ex-HDFC AMC MD, CA with blue-chip background) appears genuinely independent. Of the other three independents: Goel (Michael & Susan Dell Foundation, NBFC boards) and Karve (Mahindra Finance CFO; Added Sep 2025) bring financial expertise; Gupta (ex-Zomato Head of New Businesses) brings consumer-digital experience, though his financial-services expertise is thinner. The recently refreshed independent cohort (three of four appointed in 2024–2025) is a positive.

| Signal | Detail | Source |

| Average independent director tenure (approx.) | ~1.3 years, estimated. Barve: from 2025 (~1 yr); Goel: from Jun 2024 (~2 yrs); Gupta M.: from Jan 2025 (~1.5 yrs); Karve: from Sep 2025 (~9 months). All four independents are relatively recent appointees. | Capital IQ Board Members, current (~Jun 2026) |
| Average Bupa-NED tenure | ~7 years (Fletcher on board since 2014 — over 11 years; Davis since Jan 2026 — ~6 months). Fletcher's 11+ year tenure at this board is a staleness flag for a Bupa-nominated director: he has been on the board under the old Max Bupa name and through the ownership transition, giving him institutional memory but raising the question of entrenchment / insufficient board renewal on the promoter-nominated side. | Capital IQ Board Members, current (~Jun 2026) |
| Average executive director tenure on board | ~1.5 years on the board (all three executive directors were elevated to board roles only from 2025). Their operational tenure at the company (since April 2020) is longer but board seats are recent post-IPO appointments. | Capital IQ Board Members: "Years on Board: 2025-Present" for Mahendra and Kharbanda |

This is a material overboarding risk by any standard: SEBI's LODR (Regulation 17A) caps independent directors at 7 listed-company directorships maximum but recommends moderation. Goel's 4 listed boards plus multiple private/foundation boards is high. Karve also serves on at least 3 listed boards (Niva Bupa, Kaya, Suryoday SFB) concurrently with CFO role at Mahindra Finance — serving as an active executive and independent director simultaneously is a governance concern. Barve serves on Niva Bupa and Marico (2 listed boards), which is not excessive but Marico is a significant listed company. | Capital IQ Board Members (other boards listed for each director); SEBI LODR Reg 17A (labeled as regulatory context — inference) |
| Recent refreshment | All four independent directors joined between Jun 2024 and Sep 2025 — a near-complete independent-director refresh in 18 months, coinciding with the IPO (Nov 2024). The former independent chairman (Bhave) and two former independent directors (Pant, Mittal) left around FY2024 (low director fee of ₹1.8–2.5 lakh in FY2024 for departing members suggests part-year service). This post-IPO renewal of the full independent cohort is a positive signal that existing relationships were reset. | Capital IQ Board Members; Capital IQ Compensation Summary (FY2022–FY2025 director fees) |
| Former Company Secretary change | Rajat Sharma (former Company Secretary) was replaced by Aparna Sharma as Company Secretary & Compliance Officer, effective January 29, 2026. This is a succession within the secretarial function, not an unexplained departure — Aparna Sharma joined the Secretarial Team in June 2024 and is described as a post-IPO addition who has "been instrumental in implementing SEBI Listing and Insider Trading regulations." Not a red flag. | Capital IQ Professionals; labeled as vendor data |

**Tenure read:** The independent director bench is fresh (all in role less than 2 years) — a positive from a staleness perspective, but freshness also means these directors have limited institutional knowledge of the company's operations. The one staleness concern is Fletcher (Bupa-nominated), whose 11+ year tenure on this board, while arguably providing continuity on the promoter side, means no refresh has occurred in Bupa's representation. His concurrent role as Bupa Group CRO, chairing the Risk Committee of a Bupa subsidiary, is the structural governance risk on the board.

## 3. Related-Party Transactions & Group Leakage

**Critical data gap:** The Notes to Accounts (Ind AS 24 / IFRS 17 related-party disclosure note) from the audited Annual Report are absent from the data pool. RPT flows between Niva Bupa and the Bupa group (brand fees, reinsurance cessions, technology licensing) and between Niva Bupa and Fettle Tone LLP (Fairfax-linked) cannot be sized or tested for arm's-length pricing from primary sources.

The structural risk is real and specific: Bupa Singapore Holdings (55.35% promoter) is an active global health insurer with its own brand, technology platforms, reinsurance capacity, and management expertise. It is plausible — and commercially common in insurance JVs of this type — that Niva Bupa pays:
- A brand or trademark fee for the "Bupa" name
- A technology licensing fee for any proprietary Bupa health management or claims technology
- Reinsurance premiums ceded to a Bupa group reinsurance entity

None of these is verified or quantified from any available source. Earnings call transcripts reference Bupa as a "global partner" and "knowledge provider" but do not disclose any fee arrangement.

GWP FY26 is INR 9,433 crores. Even a 1–2% brand fee would equal INR 94–189 crores, and a 5% reinsurance commission-related RPT would be ~INR 470 crores. These numbers matter at a PAT of INR 366 crores.

| RPT Type | Amount | % of Revenue | % of PAT | % of Net Worth | Arm's Length? | Source |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|---|
| Sales to / purchases from related parties | Not disclosed | N/A | N/A | N/A | Not verified | Annual Report (Ind AS 24) — absent from pool |
| Loans / advances / guarantees to related parties | Not disclosed | N/A | N/A | N/A | Not verified | Annual Report (Ind AS 24) — absent from pool |
| Royalty / brand / management fees to promoter group | Not disclosed | N/A | N/A | N/A | Not verified | Annual Report (Ind AS 24) — absent from pool |
| Rent / other payments to promoter entities | Not disclosed | N/A | N/A | N/A | Not verified | Annual Report (Ind AS 24) — absent from pool |
| Outstanding receivables from related parties | Not disclosed | N/A | N/A | N/A | Not verified | Annual Report (Ind AS 24) — absent from pool |

**Cross-reference to disqualifier scan:** The disqualifier scan (business-model/01_disqualifier-scan.md) confirmed that no RPT exceeding 25% of revenue or expenses is evidenced from available data, but explicitly flagged that "the primary evidence to conclusively clear check #3 (RPT note) sits in the audited Annual Report that is absent from the pool." No disqualifier was triggered, but the gap was flagged as material.

**Verdict:** No material related-party transactions can be confirmed or denied from available data. The structural risk of value leakage through brand, technology, or reinsurance fees to Bupa group is the highest-priority unverified governance risk. Until the Annual Report's Ind AS 24 Note is reviewed, this cannot be resolved.

## 4. Takeover Defenses & Voting Rights

India's corporate law framework (Companies Act 2013, SEBI LODR, and IRDAI regulations) governs NIVABUPA's rights profile. The primary protection for minority shareholders comes from regulatory safeguards, not from company-specific charter provisions.

| Feature | Present? | Detail | Source |
|---|---|---|---|
| Poison pill | No | India's takeover code (SEBI SAST Regulations 2011) governs acquisitions of 25%+ stake and open-offer obligations. Standalone poison pills (rights plans) are not common in Indian listed companies and are not mentioned in any available source. | India SEBI SAST Regulations (regulatory context — inference); no contrary evidence |
| Classified / staggered board | No | Indian Companies Act 2013 does not permit staggered boards. All directors are elected by shareholders annually (or as required). IRDAI may require certain appointments (CEO, CFO) to be approved by the regulator, which is a regulatory overlay — not a staggered board. | Companies Act 2013, Sec 152 (regulatory context — inference); no contrary evidence |
| Dual-class / unequal voting | No | Niva Bupa's IPO in November 2024 was on the NSE as a conventional single-class equity. No dual-class or differential voting rights exist. India's Companies Act permits differential voting rights only to promoters within specific caps (Companies Act 2013, Sec 43) and even those require special-resolution approval; none is disclosed for NIVABUPA. | Capital IQ Public Ownership Summary (single class); Q2 FY25 transcript Nov 25, 2024, p.4 (IPO context); Companies Act 2013 (inference) |
| Majority vs plurality director voting | India standard — majority | Indian companies require a majority of shareholders to elect directors. Under Companies Act, ordinary resolutions (simple majority) apply to director elections; special resolutions (75% super-majority) apply to certain material changes including related-party transactions above a threshold. IRDAI additionally requires regulatory approval for CEO/CFO appointments. | Companies Act 2013 (regulatory — inference); IRDAI Insurance Companies Corporate Governance Guidelines (inference) |
| Shareholder ability to call meetings / act by written consent | Regulated (not freely available) | Under Companies Act 2013, shareholders holding 10%+ of voting power can requisition an Extraordinary General Meeting. SEBI LODR requires an AGM within 6 months of fiscal year end (by September 30 each year). Written resolutions / consent are not permitted for public listed companies in India (as a general rule). No special rights or restrictions mentioned for NIVABUPA specifically. | Companies Act 2013, Sec 100 (regulatory — inference); no contrary evidence |
| IRDAI-specific voting / approval requirements | Present | IRDAI must approve appointments of MD & CEO, Whole Time Directors, and CFO. The IRDAI Insurance Amendment Bill (passed Q3 FY26) now permits 100% FDI in insurance, removing the prior 74% FDI cap. This means Bupa (55.35%) can further increase its stake without regulatory restriction — which changes the minority-shareholder dynamics (Bupa could potentially move to full ownership). | Q3 FY26 transcript, Jan 29, 2026, p.5 (CEO: "the amendment bill… allows 100% FDI"); IRDAI (regulatory inference) |
| Promoter lock-in (post-IPO) | Partial — SEBI ICDR | Under SEBI ICDR Regulations, promoter shares are subject to lock-in post-IPO (typically 18 months for minimum promoter contribution; 6 months for excess). The IPO was in November 2024, so the 18-month lock-in on minimum promoter contribution would expire approximately May 2026. Fettle Tone LLP (Fairfax-linked) at 7.91% is the most likely entity to face post-lock-in selling pressure; Bupa at 55.35% has no disclosed intent to sell. | Capital IQ Public Ownership Summary (ownership %; Fettle Tone 7.91%); SEBI ICDR Regulations (inference); no lock-in schedule in data pool |

**Takeover defense summary:** No company-specific anti-shareholder defenses exist. The SEBI SAST open-offer framework protects minority shareholders against unsolicited acquisitions. The single material shift in the voting rights landscape is the passage of the Insurance Amendment Bill permitting 100% FDI — Bupa can now consolidate to full ownership without a regulatory cap. Whether this is positive (simplifying structure) or negative (squeezing out minority) depends on Bupa's future action. No evidence of any such plan.

## 5. Minority-Shareholder Protection Read

The board structure at NIVABUPA has the right form on paper but is materially compromised in substance on one dimension: the two Bupa-nominated non-executive directors — including one who is Bupa's Group Chief Risk Officer and chairs NIVABUPA's own Risk Committee — are not genuinely independent, even though they are classified as "external." Of the nine board members, only four (Barve, Goel, Gupta M., Karve) are truly independent of the promoter group. That is 44% of the board — below the spirit of SEBI's independent-director requirements for listed companies (where the target is 50%+ for listed companies with promoter > 50%). The independent chairman (Barve) is a genuine positive. The three of the four independents who joined in 2024–2025 appear qualified and non-conflicted.

The single biggest structural risk to minority holders is not the board composition per se, but the combination of: (a) a majority promoter (Bupa, 55.35%) who is simultaneously a global business partner with the potential to extract economic value through brand fees, reinsurance, and technology licensing; (b) the inability to size those flows from available data (the Annual Report's Ind AS 24 Note is absent); and (c) the fact that Bupa's own Group CRO sits on the committee structure and chairs risk oversight. This is the core leakage risk: minority holders cannot see whether Bupa is acting as a value-building promoter or as an economic counterparty extracting a below-market royalty or reinsurance spread.

The passage of the Insurance Amendment Bill (100% FDI now permitted) means Bupa's option set has expanded — it can now move toward full ownership without the regulatory constraint. This is not necessarily adverse (a full buyout at a fair price would benefit minority shareholders), but it creates uncertainty about the future minority-shareholder relationship.

**Verdict: Adequate (with material reservations).** The formal governance structure — independent chairman, genuinely independent non-executive directors in the majority of truly independent positions, chair/CEO split, stable management, no dual-class shares, no staggered board, no poison pill — is sound. However, the structural conflict from a majority promoter who is also a business-services counterparty, the Bupa-nominated Risk Committee chair, and the absence of verifiable RPT data collectively represent a meaningful unresolved governance question. This is not "weak / entrenched" (there is no evidence of self-dealing or entrenched management abusing minority holders), but it is not "strong protection" either. The candid characterization is: adequate framework, material unverified risk on promoter-related value flows, and a partially compromised committee structure via the Bupa-nominated directors.

If `04_ownership-and-insider-behavior` were to determine that Bupa's controlling ownership creates a structural misalignment with per-share value maximization (CLAUDE.md §24 Filter 6, RF-OWN-004), this verdict would need to be downgraded to "weak / entrenched" per the MODULE_RULES instruction. That determination is not yet available (the `04` output has not been produced); on current evidence, Bupa is a global strategic health insurer that appears primarily interested in the success of this business, not an extractive conglomerate — but this read is not confirmed from primary filings.

## Board & Shareholder Rights Score

| Component | Score | Max Score | Evidence |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| Board independence | 12 | 20 | Chair/CEO split (+8); 4 genuinely independent directors (+8); two Bupa-nominated NEDs who are not truly independent, incl. one chairing Risk Committee (−4); Audit and Remuneration Committees partially compromised (−0, reflected in committee quality) |
| True independence / tenure / overboarding | 10 | 20 | Fresh independent cohort (all post-2024) is a positive (+8); Goel and Karve overboarding concerns (−4); Fletcher 11-year promoter-NED tenure (−4) |
| Committee quality | 7 | 15 | Audit Committee includes Bupa-nominated Fletcher (−4); Risk Committee chaired by Bupa Group CRO (−4); Nomination/Remuneration committees partially compromised for same reason; offset by Goel (qualified independent) on Audit and Remuneration (+0); no CG Report to confirm full committee composition or terms of reference |
| RPT and group-leakage protection | 5 | 20 | No disqualifier triggered; no evidence of active RPT abuse; but Ind AS 24 Note is absent and structural RPT risk from Bupa's promoter + commercial-partner dual role is unverified (−10); Risk Committee chairman conflict (−5) |
| Shareholder voting rights | 10 | 15 | No dual-class shares, no staggered board, no poison pill; India SEBI framework provides open-offer protection; 100% FDI amendment creates new minority uncertainty (−3); AGM voting unknown (−2) |
| AGM opposition / minority protection | 3 | 10 | AGM voting not available (−5); ESOP scheme exists but size unknown (−1); no insider selling is neutral; institutional activity slightly positive (+3) |
| **Total** | **47** | **100** | Partial-data cap applies: AGM voting data not available; RPT data not available; committee composition partially disclosed only |

**Score interpretation:** 47/100 — Mixed / average governance. The score is held down primarily by: (1) the RPT data gap on Bupa-related flows (structural risk, unverifiable); (2) Fletcher's dual role as Bupa Group CRO and Risk Committee chairman; and (3) the absence of AGM voting data. The underlying framework — chair/CEO split, fresh independent directors, no anti-shareholder structural devices — would score higher if the RPT gap were resolved and committee independence improved.

**Cap applied:** "Shareholder friendliness max 60" (per MODULE_RULES partial-data rules — PIT insider-trade disclosures absent; primary shareholding-pattern filing absent; AGM voting not in pool). The raw score of 47 is already below the cap so the cap is not binding in this instance.

## management-governance / 06_candor-and-disclosure-quality.md

_Source: `06_candor-and-disclosure-quality.md`_

# Candor & Disclosure Quality — NIVABUPA

**Company:** Niva Bupa Health Insurance Company Limited (NSEI:NIVABUPA)
**Date:** 2026-06-22
**Reporting standard:** India GAAP (IRDAI insurance template) + voluntary IFRS
**Jurisdiction:** India / SEBI-LODR + IRDAI
**Upstream inputs used:** `01_management-and-track-record.md`, `earnings/06_earnings-quality.md`, `earnings/04_guidance-consensus.md`, `business-model/01_disqualifier-scan.md`

**Partial-data note:** No audited Annual Report (IRDAI statutory filing / SEBI LODR annual accounts) is in the data pool. RPT disclosures, the auditor's report, and audited cash flow notes cannot be verified at source. Candor is assessed from six earnings call transcripts (Q2 FY25 through Q4 FY26) and cross-module analysis. Components affected by the absence of a primary filing are capped below and flagged where they apply.

---

## 1. Owning the Misses

The misses identified in `01_management-and-track-record.md` that matter most for this assessment are: (a) the FQ3 FY25 EPS miss of −80%; (b) the Q1 FY26 claims auto-adjudication suspension and SLA collapse; and (c) the consistent GWP miss versus street consensus across all six quarters where data exists.

| Miss (from 01) | How It Was Communicated | Owned or Obscured? | Source |
|---|---|---|---|
| FQ3 FY25 EPS: ₹0.07 actual vs ₹0.35 consensus (−80%) | CEO opened the Q3 FY25 call by front-loading the accounting transition context before presenting any numbers: "Q3 for the entire industry and indeed for us was a quarter of transition… the change is about accounting and therefore does not have a material bearing on economic value." CFO then gave both IGAAP and IFRS PAT numbers (IFRS PAT tripled from ₹4.6 cr to ₹13.2 cr on a like-for-like 9-month basis), and separately reported the IGAAP 1/N distorted figure. The explanation was consistent with what was promised in prior quarters. No adjustments were made to flatter the number beyond providing the IFRS alternative, which is the regulator-sanctioned primary metric. | Owned with explanation — structural accounting context provided proactively and consistently; explanation borne out by subsequent recovery. Mild caveat: the distinction between IGAAP (which produced the −80% miss) and IFRS (which shows improving profit) requires investors to follow two accounting bases simultaneously, and the IGAAP miss was the headline figure for consensus. | Q3 FY25 transcript, Feb 4, 2025, pp. 4–5 (CEO prepared remarks); Q4 FY25 transcript, May 7, 2025, p.5 (full-year context); earnings/06_earnings-quality.md (1/N accounting discussion) |
| Q1 FY26 claims auto-adjudication suspension; SLA dropped from 90%+ to 76% within-30-minute cashless approvals; reserve build-up | CEO disclosed proactively in prepared remarks: "there is one metric that did go south in Q1, specifically on claims auto-adjudication. On account of a bunch of information security assurance reviews specifically with third parties, we did suspend the auto-adjudication service." CFO followed with specific quantification: loss ratio increased by around 2% "largely on account of strengthening of reserves." CEO confirmed the system was restored in Q2 (July 2025) on the same call. The root cause — what the information security review found — was not described. | Partially owned: the disruption itself was disclosed proactively and quantified, which is a transparency positive. However, the nature of the security vulnerability, whether customer data was accessed, and whether IRDAI was notified were not disclosed. Calling it an "information security assurance review with third parties" is technically accurate but avoids stating whether a breach occurred. This is disclosure that meets the minimum bar without going further. | Q1 FY26 transcript, Jul 31, 2025, pp. 4–6 (CEO and CFO prepared remarks) |
| GWP / revenue miss: −8.7% vs consensus FY25; −6.2% FY26; miss in all six quarters where revenue comparison is available | Management never formally guided GWP and does not issue point guidance, so these are consensus vs outcome gaps rather than promise vs delivery gaps in the strict sense. When analysts reference a 25% growth assumption, management does not dispute it — CEO says only "broadly our view on this has not changed" without correcting or narrowing a specific number. This is ambiguous guidance — not false, but it leaves analysts free to set numbers management knows may be high. | Mixed: management is not lying; it sets no formal guidance. But it also does not correct implicitly high street estimates. The consistent 6–9% GWP miss over two full years and all quarterly periods suggests the market is systematically calibrated above the company's own internal view, and management has not acted to reset it. This is passive rather than active misleading, but it is a pattern of insufficient correction. | earnings/04_guidance-consensus.md (beat/miss pattern); Q4 FY26 transcript, May 8, 2026, p.6 (CEO response to analyst's 25% growth assumption) |
| Combined ratio FY26: 101.4%, a tick-up of 20 basis points vs FY25's 101.2%, moving away from the 99% FY2029 target | CFO stated plainly on the Q4 FY26 call: "While there is increase in overall loss ratio by 1.1%, primarily due to mix change, this has been more than offset by reduction in expense ratio by 2.7%." The combined ratio improvement (stated as 160 bps improvement full year) referenced the comparison against a full FY24 reference rather than FY25, which is technically correct but flatters the presentation — the Q4 FY26 combined ratio versus FY25 (101.2%) was essentially flat to slightly worse. The FY2029 99% target was restated without revision. | Mixed: the metric was disclosed (no hiding), but the comparison base chosen (FY24 vs FY25) obscures the stall in FY26 vs FY25 progress. An analyst would catch this; a casual reader would not. No adjustment to the FY2029 target despite the FY26 stall is aspirationally consistent but would be more credible with an updated bridge showing how 250+ basis points are achieved in three years. | Q4 FY26 transcript, May 8, 2026, p.5 (CFO: "combined ratio for FY '26 under IFRS has improved by 160 basis points to 101.4%"); Q4 FY25 transcript, May 7, 2025, p.5 (101.2% FY25) |

---

## 2. Non-GAAP / Adjustment Aggressiveness

Cross-referenced against `earnings/06_earnings-quality.md`. The earnings quality module awarded a score of 62/100 and identified one significant accounting complexity: the dual IGAAP / IFRS reporting. No formal non-GAAP earnings reconciliation exists in the standard sense, but two full sets of accounts are published.

| Signal | Detail | Source |
|---|---|---|
| Recurring "one-off" addbacks | No recurring addbacks in the typical industrial-company sense. The only genuine one-off addback is the FY25 CFO spike (₹16,753 mn vs normalised ~₹8,800 mn) from the IRDAI-mandated 1/N accounting transition. Management explicitly and repeatedly flagged this as non-recurring in Q1 FY26 and Q4 FY26. The Q3 FY26 Labour Code past service cost (₹20 crores) was separately called out as a genuine one-time regulatory charge. The EOM policyholder-to-shareholder reversal in Q3/Q4 FY26 was correctly described as a "contra entry" with no P&L impact — an optical-only item. None of these are recurring one-offs that flatter earnings. The structural intra-year EPS pattern (Q1–Q3 losses, Q4 profits under IGAAP) is not a one-off — it is the signature of the 1/N rule and will repeat every year until IFRS 17 replaces IGAAP in FY27. Management has consistently and correctly explained this. | earnings/06_earnings-quality.md, Section 5 (One-Off Items); Q3 FY26 transcript, Jan 29, 2026, p.5; Q4 FY26 transcript, May 8, 2026, pp. 7–8 |
| GAAP-to-adjusted gap (magnitude / trend) | Full-year IGAAP PAT FY26 and IFRS PAT FY26 are virtually identical (₹3,661 mn vs ₹3,660 mn). At the full-year level, the gap is near zero. The large gap appears only intra-year (Q1–Q3 IGAAP shows losses; Q1–Q3 IFRS shows profits), and management has explained this consistently across all six calls. The Capital IQ normalized EPS adjustment (₹1.98 reported IGAAP vs ₹0.71 normalized) is a data-vendor construct whose composition is not fully transparent from available data — this is a data limitation rather than evidence of management manipulation. The gap is structural (regulatory accounting), not discretionary. | earnings/06_earnings-quality.md, Section 7 (Reported vs Adjusted Reconciliation); Q4 FY26 transcript, May 8, 2026, p.5 |
| Does adjusted framing flatter reality? | The IFRS presentation is management's primary operating metric and is the accounting standard the company and its parent Bupa use globally. Presenting IFRS as the more meaningful number is not spin — it is the same approach Bupa uses for its own group accounts. The company publishes both full sets of accounts, not just the better-looking one. However, in all investor-facing communications, management leads with IFRS (where all quarterly periods show positive PAT) rather than IGAAP (where Q1–Q3 show losses). The IFRS lead framing is appropriate and disclosed, but consistently leading with the more favourable standard, while never denying IGAAP, is a mild framing choice. The FY26 intangible capex jump (₹430 mn, +343% YoY) has not been discussed in depth on any call — IT project spending is mentioned but capitalisation rates and useful lives are not addressed. | earnings/06_earnings-quality.md, Sections 4 and 6; Q1 FY26 transcript, Jul 31, 2025, p.5 (IT systems named); Q4 FY26 transcript, May 8, 2026, p.5 |

**Adjustment aggressiveness verdict: conservative / not aggressive.** The accounting complexity at Niva Bupa is structural and regulatory (IRDAI 1/N mandate, dual-basis reporting), not a management choice designed to flatter results. Management's IFRS preference is disclosed, consistent, and aligned with their parent's own accounting standards. No recurring "one-off" addbacks have been identified. The GAAP-to-adjusted gap washes out at the full-year level. Non-GAAP aggressiveness is low.

---

## 3. Disclosure Transparency

Management provides consistent, specific KPI disclosure across all six calls. Each quarter, the CEO presents: GWP growth on a like-for-like (ex-1/N) basis, IFRS PAT, combined ratio (IFRS), loss ratio and expense ratio decomposed, EOM ratio, retail market share, solvency ratio, investment AUM and yield, NPS across 25 touch points, auto-adjudication rate, and channel mix. These are the KPIs that actually drive value for a health insurer scaling toward underwriting profitability. The disclosure set has been consistent across all six post-IPO quarters, and in Q4 FY26 the CFO also quantified segment loss ratios (group health 60.5%, retail health improving each quarter from 68.1% H1 to 66.8% FY26) when asked directly. Loss ratio by segment is disclosed, though the group vs retail segment P&L is not separately published as a standalone segment report.

The one area that has become less transparent over time is the claims auto-adjudication rate, which was a feature KPI in Q2 FY25 (cited as 28%) and Q3 FY25 (28.6%), disappeared from the Q1 FY26 call during the suspension (management disclosed the suspension but did not restate the metric), and was not highlighted as prominently in subsequent calls. This is not a material concealment — the suspension was disclosed — but the cadence of reporting on a previously prominent KPI changed at the moment the metric declined. The FY26 intangible capex jump (₹430 mn, +343%) is mentioned in the context of named IT systems (Oracle Health, Sprinklr, Convin AI) but capitalisation methodology is not described — verifiable only from the primary annual report that is absent from the data pool.

**The most significant transparency gap is the absence of RPT disclosure.** Bupa Singapore, a promoter, plausibly receives brand royalties, reinsurance payments, and technology licence fees from Niva Bupa. None of these flows have been quantified or confirmed arm's-length on any transcript, and the primary annual report with the Ind AS 24 related-party note is not available. This is a data sufficiency gap rather than a disclosed concealment, but it is the largest missing piece in the overall transparency picture.

---

## 4. Tone in Bad Times

The worst recent period in terms of reported numbers is Q3 FY25 (Feb 4, 2025): the company was freshly listed (November 2024), facing its first post-IPO earnings call, with a reported EPS of ₹0.07 against a ₹0.35 consensus — an 80% miss under the headline normalized metric. CEO Ramachandran's tone on that call was direct: he opened by naming the accounting change explicitly, framed it as an industry-wide event, stated what it meant and what it did not mean for economic value, and confirmed the underlying IFRS PAT had tripled quarter-on-quarter. He did not avoid the question. The CFO provided both accounting bases side by side with enough precision that analysts could reconstruct the figures. The Q&A section shows analysts drilling into loss ratio decomposition, commission accounting mechanics, and regulatory glide path — and management answered all of these directly, including providing numerical breakdowns (9M loss ratio at 64.2% on IFRS, retail 67%, overall 64.2%).

Q1 FY26 (Jul 31, 2025) is the second worst period — the claims SLA miss was disclosed proactively in the CEO's prepared remarks, not in response to an analyst question. Critically, management separately flagged that Q1 FY26 had experienced a reserve build-up (loss ratio rise) because of the auto-adjudication suspension, quantified the SLA decline (90% to 76%), and confirmed the resolution timeline. The Q&A on that call shows analysts pressing on the loss ratio drivers, reserve adequacy, and whether the trend signals broader incidence-rate shifts. Management answered each question with numbers (retail loss ratio 68%, group 61%, prior year retail 66%, group 58%). The CFO did not deflect questions about the reserve strengthening — he confirmed it was a prudent response to the suspension and forecast stabilisation by year-end. This is straightforward Q&A, not evasion.

The consistent pattern across bad periods: management leads with IFRS to contextualise IGAAP distortions, discloses operational problems in prepared remarks rather than waiting for analyst questions, and answers Q&A with specific numbers. There is no pattern of deflecting, going to "offline" for substantive questions (one analyst question on IFRS reconciliation was briefly deferred to offline, which is acceptable and standard), or answering qualitatively when quantitative data was available.

---

## 5. Candor Read

Niva Bupa's management, led by CEO Ramachandran and CFO Mahendra, has a consistent record of communicating bad news directly: the FQ3 FY25 −80% EPS miss was framed in its structural accounting context before any analyst asked, the Q1 FY26 claims disruption was disclosed in prepared remarks with specific SLA numbers, and Q&A across all six calls shows management answering pointed questions with figures rather than narratives. Non-GAAP aggressiveness is low — the dual IGAAP / IFRS reporting reflects regulatory mandate, not earnings management, and the full-year GAAP-to-adjusted gap is near zero. The biggest candor limitation is structural: the audited Annual Report is absent from the data pool, so RPT flows with Bupa Singapore (brand, reinsurance, technology) are unverified, and management has not voluntarily quantified these on any call. The combined ratio comparison base chosen in Q4 FY26 (versus FY24 rather than FY25) mildly flatters the FY26 progress narrative, and the failure to proactively correct the consistently high street GWP estimates is a passive transparency shortfall.

**Verdict: candid / high-trust** — with one important caveat. On every miss that has occurred in the observable window, management disclosed it proactively, explained it with numbers, and took Q&A directly. The non-GAAP picture is not aggressive. The trust limitation is the unverified RPT exposure with Bupa Singapore, which is a data-sufficiency gap rather than an active concealment but which the audited Annual Report alone can resolve. Until that filing is reviewed, a small residual confidence reduction is appropriate. The single biggest candor signal is the Q1 FY26 claims auto-adjudication suspension disclosure: management named the failure, quantified the SLA decline, and explained the reserve impact in the same prepared-remarks paragraph that described every other positive metric — this is what candid communication looks like.

**Partial-data cap note:** The RPT disclosure component (06-010) cannot be scored — Insufficient Data is applied. If material RPTs with Bupa Singapore were disclosed and arm's-length confirmed in the primary annual report, the score would not change materially. If material undisclosed RPTs were found, the KPI consistency and candor read would be revised downward and the RF-RPT-001 flag would be triggered. The score of 87 is a ceiling on currently available evidence.
